Talk by Dr. Xie Shou Kang

Dr. Xie Shou Kang, the Chargé d'affaires in Belgium, returned to China on the 10th of this month,

as previously reported. Now that Mr. Xie has come to Shanghai for business, a reporter visited him at the residence of Mr. Shao Goumei and recorded his remarks as follows: (Question) What is the situation of the overseas Chinese in Belgium? (Answer) There are about six hundred Chinese in Belgium, half of whom are students and half of whom are sailors. (Question) What kind of academic subjects do students in Belgium mostly study? (Answer) Belgium is an industrial country, and most of the Chinese students in Belgium study industry. Recently, some have also studied fine arts, and most of them are diligent and have excellent grades. (Question) What is the situation of the sailors? (Answer) The so-called sailors refer to the Chinese laborers engaged in navigation. They do not come and go regularly, but because of their large number, there are often about three hundred people in Antwerp (Anevss), a major port in Belgium. (Question) It is said that the unemployment problem in Europe is serious. Are these overseas Chinese affected? (Answer) The unemployment problem is a widespread problem, and sailors in Belgium are no exception. Therefore, I reported the details to the central government last year. The central government cared about the overseas Chinese and sent funds for relief. However, the situation is gradually easing now. Some of our country's sailors have changed their occupation to bricklayers, and their monthly wages can reach two hundred yuan. (Question) During your year abroad, you spared no effort in promoting the new atmosphere of China and its ancient culture. The European newspapers praised you unanimously on that day, but only a glimpse of it has been seen in the Chinese newspapers. Can we hear more about the details? (Answer) I feel that I am superficial and dare not say that I have achieved any great results. However, when I was in Belgium, I

Page 14

never closed myself off from any activities that I should participate in. As for the lectures invited by various cultural institutions in France and Germany, such as the Paris Chamber of Deputies, the China-France Friendship Group, the French National Broadcasting Radio Station, the International Cultural Cooperation Society, and the International Friendship Association, as well as the University of Frankfurt in Germany, I took the opportunity to promote our country, which seems to be what I should do. (Question) What works have you published in recent years? (Answer) I was very busy with official duties in Belgium, and my personal work was suspended. However, the "Belgium Bookstore" asked to compile and publish my lectures and essays from various places, titled E st Ouest R eflets Croises, and received long prefaces from the Belgian Foreign Minister Paul Homans (which seems to have been translated and published in Chinese newspapers) and the Belgian literary figure Vanzypl. It will be published in October of this year. (Question) How was Xu Beihong's exhibition in Brussels? (Answer) Xu's works already have a considerable status in Europe, and many people in the art world know about him. Therefore, this exhibition was particularly successful. The Minister of Education personally attended the opening ceremony, and the Queen of Belgium inquired about the artist's life when she visited the exhibition. It is still a groundbreaking achievement for Chinese artists to have such success abroad. (Question) What are your thoughts on returning to China? Disaster is striking China's survival and is striking the world's civilization. The situation is serious, and the whole country should work together to eliminate it and win back our true freedom to achieve the goal of the revolution.

Dr. Wu Lien-teh's Talk After Returning to China

▲ The Situation of Attending the International Three Important Meetings

▲ Optimism for the Future of Epidemic Prevention

Dr. Wu Lien-teh, Director of the National Seaport Epidemic Prevention Office of the Ministry of Health, has returned to China after completing his mission of attending the three important meetings of the Health Administration and Narcotics of the League of Nations in Europe. He arrived in Shanghai at about 5 pm the day before yesterday. A reporter from the New Sound News Agency paid a special visit yesterday. The following is a record of his remarks regarding the situation of attending the three important international conferences.

▲ Health Committee Wu said that he left the country on April 11, went to Europe via Siberia, and arrived in Geneva on the 27th to attend the Health Committee of the League of Nations, the 63rd International Administrative Conference, and the most important World Narcotics Conference. The Health Committee only reported on the progress of health in our country and the annual expenses of our government on health matters. In the past, the annual expenses on health matters in our country were only more than one million yuan, but recently it has increased to more than three million yuan, which shows the gradual progress of health affairs in our country.

▲ Sending Personnel to China The 63rd International Administrative Conference of the League of Nations was held in Geneva on May 17. There were a total of 14 attendees, including the foreign ministers of various countries. I attended as a representative of Finance Minister Song Ziwen, requesting that they send commissioners to China to assist our country in the three tasks of finance, transportation, and education in an advisory capacity and nature. The League of Nations has now agreed and will send them to China in three groups. Each group will have about three people. The first group will send an education commissioner first, who is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on September 1. The commissioners of the finance and transportation groups have not yet been determined, but it is expected that they will be decided soon and will come to China immediately.

▲ Narcotics At the International Narcotics Conference, which began on May 17 and ended on July 13, there were a large number of representatives from various countries, a total of 54 countries. The most vigorous discussions at the meeting were on narcotics such as heroin. Representatives from various countries considered that this kind of narcotic substance originated in the six countries of Britain, the United States, France, Germany, the Netherlands, and Switzerland, and that China, India, and Egypt were the main countries suffering from its harm. Therefore, I proposed to ban the manufacture of heroin in various countries. At the same time, representatives from Japan, the Soviet Union, and other countries also opposed the manufacture and sale of heroin by the six countries of Britain, the United States, France, and Germany. As a result, due to the many uses in the medical and chemical industries, the complete ban was not passed, but the manufacture limited to the use of the medical and chemical industries was passed, and 28 countries signed the resolution not to manufacture it for any purpose other than medical and chemical uses.

▲ Opium Conference Because the discussion on opium narcotics is more related to the East, it was decided to hold the World Opium Conference in Siam on November 7. At that time, I am afraid that I will not be able to attend, or the government will send another representative to participate.

▲ Epidemic Prevention Situation Wu said at the end that when he returned to China from Marseille, he observed the commercial situation of various countries along the way in France, Italy, India, Singapore, the Philippines, and Hong Kong, which was extremely bleak. After arriving in China, he also inspected the epidemic prevention situation of the southern seaports of our country in Shantou, Xiamen, etc., which was very good. Since our country took back the epidemic prevention work from the hands of foreigners and ran it ourselves, there has been rapid progress. Now that this work has only been taken back for six months, there are facilities such as institutes. There was no such achievement in the hands of foreigners for several years, which shows that if our country does not seek progress in everything, it is easy to seek progress.

Wusong Water Police Fourth District Ordered to Investigate and Prohibit Rice Export

Jiang Chao Xiong, the chief of the fourth district of the Wusong Maritime Provincial Public Security Team of Jiangsu, received an order from the Department of Civil Affairs of the Jiangsu Provincial Government yesterday, stating that the smuggling of rice out of the province has been strictly prohibited on record. This year's moldy rain has been continuous, and the famine has become apparent. Now is the time when the new and old crops are not yet available, and the market price is rising daily. The ban should be reiterated to maintain the people's food supply. He ordered to supervise and strictly investigate and prohibit any negligence. After receiving the order, District Chief Jiang considered that Wusong Port is an important gateway to the rivers and seas, and there may be unscrupulous merchants smuggling rice for export. He has ordered Zhang Zongliang, the captain of the Sixteenth Team, Gong Mianqin, the captain of the Seventeenth Team, and Xie Ze Zhi, the captain of the Eighteenth Team, to add patrol boats from now on, to distribute them outside the port and at the key routes of the boat companies, and to strictly investigate and arrest.

Foreign Wheat Orders Should Be Registered Immediately

The Shanghai Chinese Grain, Oilcake, and Allied Trades Association issued a public notice to all members yesterday, stating that it had recently received an instruction from the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, stating that a new wheat crop has been launched on the market, and it is said that merchants are still ordering foreign wheat, which not only causes prices to fall, but also causes the pain of having nothing to sell. It must be known that purchasing foreign goods was originally a remedy for when the local products were insufficient. Now that local wheat is available, there is no need to seek foreign supplies. If the industry believes that domestic wheat has not been strictly inspected and the goods are mixed and unclean, it can try to rectify it and request government assistance. How can it be abandoned because of choking, and not consider the farmers and domestic products? The merchants of the industry have always known the big picture and should jointly plan to maintain domestic wheat production and rectification and improvement methods, so that farmers and merchants can benefit from both. In addition to issuing separate orders, it is hereby ordered that you comply with the instructions and urge the industry to register the foreign wheat that has been ordered with the Bureau as soon as possible, which is of utmost importance. This order, etc. Upon receipt of this, it should be recorded and instructed, and it is hoped that all members of the industry will be informed and strictly implement it. This is hereby announced.

The Initiation of the China Law Society

The preparatory committee of the China Law Society sent a public letter to all levels of courts across the country, bar associations in various provinces, and law schools yesterday, stating that the Chinese legal system is one of the five major legal systems in the world, with deep roots and flourishing branches. In addition to the Chinese nation, those who are subject to its control include Korea, Japan, Annam, and even Myanmar, Siam, and the South Seas Islands, all of which are directly and indirectly blessed by it. Its historical glory is long-standing, and it is unparalleled in the world's legal systems. Only because of environmental changes, legal practitioners often ignore the spirit of the evolution of the times, stick to conventions, and allow the power of this great legal system to wither day by day. Since the revolution, people from all walks of life have vigorously reversed the past, only respecting imported legal studies, and thus allowing hundreds of millions of Chinese people to be completely immersed in imported legal systems. Although the world is becoming more and more unified, promoting the inherent spirit of the nation is something that the entire nation should have. Now, in the context of the establishment of the country based on the Three Principles of the People, the sorting out and creation of new and old laws in the country, and the comparative analysis of academic theories abroad, all the more need legal scholars to conduct in-depth research before they can be of help. In recent years, the China Engineering Society and the China Economic Society have gathered experts together, and they have been able to provide significant contributions in academics. At this time of the succession of the new and the old, how dare the people in our legal field underestimate ourselves? Therefore, we are uniting with comrades to initiate the organization of the China Law Society, intending to gather judges, lawyers, professors of law, politics, and other subjects, and students of law and political science who have graduated from all over the country, to do their best according to their knowledge and abilities, and according to their positions, to conduct deeper research on various laws and regulations of the past, present, and foreign countries, in order to promote the Chinese legal system, and to integrate it with the major legal systems of the world, and thereby to promote the highest laws that adapt to our country's nation-building ideology and suit the common life of our nation. However, this matter is of great importance, and it cannot be achieved without the combined efforts of all the wise men. We have long admired your court, association, and school for your in-depth study of law and outstanding reputation. If you are willing to join the initiative, then one call will be followed by a hundred responses. The prosperity of law is deeply relied upon. If you agree, please reply immediately. We look forward to it in anticipation. We are in haste to inform you and wish you a peaceful summer. To so and so, Zhang Yaozeng, Chu Fucheng, Wang Youling, Wan Zhaozhi, Liu Lushi, Wu Jingxiong, Chen Zemin, Guo Wei, Xu Jiashi, Dai Xiuzan, Qin Liankui, Tan Yigong, Li Shirui, Liu Zuwang, Liu Tuxiong, Shen Junru, Lu Dingkui, Yu Zhongluo, Lu Shaozong, Zhao Zuwei, Jiang Yiping, Wu Chengyu, Zhang Zhirang, Zhao Chen, Pan Zhenya, Sheng Zhenwei, Wang Zhenshen, Yang Binbin, Cai Nipei, Zhang Enhua, Shan Yuhua, Zhong Hongsheng, Huang Han, Wu Zhiping, Zhang Zhengxue, Zhang Feixiong, Zhou Shiyun, and others.

Introducing the "Northeast Yearbook"

The Northeast Yearbook published by the Northeast Cultural Society is richly collected. The organizer spent years and years of time, borrowed the power of the political, military, academic, and commercial circles of the four provinces, and referred to hundreds of specialized writings. It also carefully edited and arranged based on detailed tables from various sources, indicating the source. Only then could this grand view be achieved, fully revealing the far-reaching progress of various political and social phenomena in the Northeast in recent years within this small compilation. It is truly a book that those who study the Northeast issue cannot be without.

Customs Auctions Should Be Handed Over to Chinese Merchants

▲ Municipal Chamber of Commerce Sends Letter to Jianghai Customs Administration

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Jianghai Customs Supervisor's Office yesterday regarding the matter of customs auctions being exclusively handed over to Chinese merchants, stating that the letter from the Chinese Yizhong Auction House, a member of the Chamber of Commerce, received on the 25th of this month, stated that the auction industry is impartial and has the nature of arbitration, which is different from ordinary commercial organizations. Therefore, its business has strict regulations. In the past, Chinese merchants did not know how to organize, so foreign merchants invaded. Not only were the rights and interests lost, but also the national dignity was tarnished. The members established the Chinese Yizhong Auction House in 1927 and immediately submitted applications to the Shanghai Political Branch, the Shanghai Municipal Agricultural and Industrial Chamber of Commerce, the National Registration Bureau, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and the various levels of courts. The former Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce approved the establishment and distributed protection and promotion, which are all on file. The members' acquisition of auction qualifications is purely legal. Later, the members were invited by the various levels of courts as appraisers and by various commercial organizations as notaries public, and the procedures were handled in an orderly manner. However, the Jianghai Customs Office has always rotated the auction of goods from Lu Yisimo Foreign Firm and Ruihe Foreign Firm. After the establishment of the Shanghai Provisional Court, the members requested the Customs to join the auction rotation, following the example of the Court's auction rotation, and jointly participated in the handling with the two foreign firms. Later, the Provisional Court was changed to the Special Zone Court. All civil appraisal and valuation affairs were handled by Chinese merchants, and foreign merchants did not participate, which was intended to safeguard legal rights and consolidate the national system. Now that legal rights have been recovered, all businesses related to national sovereignty should be handled by Chinese people themselves. The Customs should take back its autonomy and, for the business of auctioning confiscated goods, should designate Chinese merchants to handle it exclusively and no longer allow foreign merchants to be mixed in, dividing the sovereignty. Therefore, a special letter is prepared and submitted to your office for forwarding to the Jianghai Customs, requesting that the foreign merchant's auction rotation be immediately cancelled and handled exclusively by the legal Chinese auction house in order to maintain the national system and protect sovereignty. After investigation, the Customs is a national administrative agency, and although it handles tax collection and other matters, it has more contact with foreign merchants, which is the same as the Special Zone's acceptance of Chinese and foreign lawsuits. Since the Shanghai Provisional Court was reorganized into the Special Zone Court, all the old precedents of the former Chinese and foreign merchants' auction rotation have been abandoned and changed to the Chinese Yizhong Auction House's exclusive undertaking, which has been implemented for a long time and has not been hindered. Then, the Customs should follow the example of the Special Zone Court for auctioning confiscated items and change it to the exclusive handling by Chinese merchants.

Undertaking, there is no so-called conflict. Maintaining domestic chambers of commerce is a common policy of any country, and national institutions must be able to implement it effectively in order to achieve the effect of speaking and acting. A letter is hereby prepared and submitted, and it is hoped that your office will consult with the tax division and promptly implement it in order to establish public friendship.

Judicial Yuan Interprets Article 5 of the Chamber of Commerce Law

▲ The Law is Based on the Recognition of the Central Training Department

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce received a telegram from the Judicial Yuan yesterday, stating that the telegram from Qiaodai and the deletion telegram from the Wusong Chamber of Commerce are both known. After investigating the provisions of Article 5 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, but in prosperous areas and towns, chambers of commerce may also be established separately or jointly. The so-called "may be established" does not mean that they must be established. Since the Wusong Chamber of Commerce has been deemed by the Central Training Department in accordance with the Chamber of Commerce Law to not need to be established separately, there is no need to explain it further. Inform them by telegram and ask them to forward it to the Wusong Chamber of Commerce. Sincerely printed by the Judicial Yuan.

Wusong Electricity Went Out Last Morning

At about 2:40 am yesterday, the lights in the Wusong area suddenly went out completely, turning into a dark world. After about an hour, it began to light up again, and then it flickered on and off for about half an hour before it returned to normal. Fortunately, the sky was not bright when the lights went out, and the residents were all asleep. It happened to be raining, so there were no pedestrians on the road. Except for the Seventh District Public Security Police, who patrolled the area with a little more attention, there were no other actions. It was learned that the current used by the Wusong Baoming Electric Company is completely fed by the Yinhang Hydropower Plant. The company does not generate electricity. Yesterday, it was due to the damage to the machinery of the Hydropower Plant. It has now been completely repaired.

Chen Zonghan's Report on Attending the U.S. National Electric Light Association Convention

The U.S. National Electric Light Association held its 54th annual convention in Atlantic City from June 8th to 12th of this year. The Chinese National Private Electric Industry Association was invited to send representatives. Due to the short notice, Mr. Chen Zonghan, an electrical engineering expert residing in the United States, was immediately telegraphed to attend. This has been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that after the convention, Mr. Chen sent a detailed report to the Shanghai office of the National Private Electric Industry Association. The report includes the following three items: (1) A brief history and organization of the Association. The Association was founded in 1885 and has a history of 46 years. Membership is divided into nine categories. The headquarters has a President, Vice President, Secretary, and Treasurer. The National Executive Committee is the highest governing body. Below that are Special and General Committees, and several sections. Currently, there are four sections: Planning, Commercial, Engineering, and Public Relations. Each section has a committee and several subcommittees. Provincial branches are established in each province, and several provincial branches form a district branch. The forty-eight states of the United States are divided into twelve districts, plus one district in Canada, for a total of thirteen districts. Nine sub-branches are established. A company or town with more than ten members can establish a branch. (2) The Association's affairs. The Association's purpose is to promote the science and technology of electricity generation, distribution, and application. All its activities are purely educational and research-oriented. The duties of the committees and sections are defined by the National Executive Committee based on their nature and scope. For external activities, the President appoints representatives to participate. The working reports of various academic organizations, government and other industrial research opportunities, international electric industry organizations and committees, and various sections are printed as separate publications from time to time, and compiled into annual convention proceedings. In addition, a monthly association publication is issued, and several specialized reference books on electricity meters, wiring fees, etc., are compiled. (3) The situation of this year's convention and electrical appliance exposition. The convention lasted four and a half days. The first day was for the executive committee meetings of each section. The remaining three and a half days were for four general assembly meetings. The Planning, Commercial, Engineering, Public Relations sections, as well as the Public Policy Committee and the Women's Committee, each held one meeting. The fourth day was designated as Edison Day to honor the inventor Edison. At each meeting, in addition to short reports from the committees or sections, there were speeches by guests or members. At the last general assembly, awards were presented and the next term's officers were elected. The topics of the speeches were mostly focused on the two most urgent issues of the moment: one was the causes and remedies for the economic depression of the past two years, and the other was the issue of public versus private ownership of the electric industry. The exposition and the convention coincided, with more than 200 participating manufacturing companies displaying a wide variety of household electrical appliances. It is said that the report will be published in full in Volume 2, Issue 1 of the Electrical Industry Quarterly. Those interested in the electric industry should read it as soon as possible.

▲ 15th District Branch: The 15th District Branch of the City Federation sent a letter to the Public Works Department regarding the relocation of the night soil depot, stating: "To the esteemed director, We have received a letter from members Dechang, Ruikang, and Tairui, stating that they reside on the North Suzhou Road near the Old Zha Gate Bridge, at numbers 596 to 599. In recent years, their businesses have flourished, and there is a significant amount of people coming and going. Unclean areas should be demolished to improve sanitation. However, the Public Works Department has a night soil depot in this area, which is detrimental to sanitation. From morning to night, a foul odor permeates the air, causing nausea. Passersby cannot help but cover their noses. Our businesses are nearby and suffer from this offensive smell, which is difficult to bear. We had initially intended to petition your department to negotiate with the Public Works Department to relocate it to another location, or to merge it with the sparsely populated Sikh Temple depot. However, we heard that the Public Works Department had already proposed relocating it, so we temporarily suspended our efforts. We request that your department and our members negotiate to have it relocated within a specified time to maintain our businesses and improve the city's appearance. Accordingly, we find that the Suzhou Road area near the depot is a vital transportation route and a central commercial hub. As businesses are located within the concession, municipal regulations prioritize cleanliness for business operations. The night soil depot, with its foul odor, not only affects commerce but also obstructs traffic. The municipal authorities should pay attention to this. We request that your department instruct the sanitation department to relocate it to the west of the Old Garbage Bridge or another location as soon as possible, to benefit commerce and facilitate transportation. With deepest respect, [addressed to] the Director General of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement."

An Innocent Person Sacrificed in the Assassination Attempt

▲ Zhang Agen Struck by a Stray Bullet

▲ Succumbs to Injuries Yesterday

On the morning of the 23rd of this month, a violent assassination attempt on the Minister of Finance of the National Government, Mr. Song Ziwen, occurred at the North Railway Station. The exchange of gunfire between Mr. Song's bodyguards and the assassins, and the resulting injuries to multiple people, have been reported in detail in this newspaper. Zhang Agen, a 54-year-old man from Suzhou, who made a living selling second-hand goods and lived at No. 672 Xiangxin Lane, Mou Su Road, went to the North Station at 7:07 AM that morning to purchase a train ticket to Suzhou. While he was buying the ticket, he suddenly heard the sounds of bombs and guns and turned to flee. Unfortunately, he was caught in the crossfire and struck by a bullet in the waist. He immediately collapsed to the ground. A police officer noticed him and immediately had him transported to Tongren Hospital for treatment. However, due to the severity of his injuries and his advanced age, he could not be saved. He died at 8:10 PM on the 25th. His body was transported by police car to the Philen Road Morgue. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo Wei of the Special District Court arrived at the morgue and confirmed that the body had been killed by a stray bullet. He then took his seat in the courtroom and inquired about the facts. Later, the deceased's son-in-law, Zhang Boying, filed a case, requesting the release of the body. Mr. Guo then ordered that Zhang Agen's body be released to his son-in-law for burial.

Lawyer Tan Yigong Raises Objections to the Sudden Conversion to Private Sale of Huang Chu Jiu's Estate

A letter from lawyer Tan Yigong states: "Regarding the liquidation of Gongfa Company and the Huang Chu Jiu family's assets, the sudden change from public auction to private sale has a significant impact on the interests of creditors and the Huang family. I have already, on behalf of the Huang family, filed an objection with the French Concession Court, along with a legal opinion. The details of this process are of interest to those concerned about this matter and general creditors. I am sending the original objection and opinion to your newspaper for appropriate publication for public viewing." The statement of objection is as follows:

▲ Statement of Objection: Regarding the liquidation of the Huang Chu Jiu estate and debts, on July 18th of this year, Your Court issued an order stating that the auction method had encountered difficulties, and the creditor representatives were also eager to expedite the conclusion of the matter for the benefit of the creditors. They applied for a change of method, continuing to use the private sale method. The two auctions were both rescinded. The liquidator should seek to sell the assets at the highest bid price. Any further discussion is unnecessary. Upon reading this order, the applicant was shocked and astonished. Your Court's order was based on the report of Gongfa Company liquidators Wu Cheng and Pan Zhaobang, both accountants, dated July 17th, and the on-court application of Jiang Yiping and other lawyers representing the creditors of Gongfa Company. The accountants' report and the lawyers' request both infringe upon rights and violate the law. The applicant cannot acknowledge them. Therefore, an objection is hereby filed in accordance with the law, with the following details: (1) Objections to the report of accountants Wu Cheng and Pan Zhaobang: This case of liquidating the Huang Chu Jiu estate and debts was submitted to Your Court for approval, and liquidators Wu and Pan of Gongfa Company were appointed to work with the applicant to properly devise a plan and report it for verification and decision. The accountants were in a supervisory and liquidating position, which is very clear. Previously, the shops exclusively owned by Huang Chu Jiu were all handled and negotiated by the accountants, and the sales contracts were drafted by the accountants and only sent to the applicant for countersignature and stamping (as evidenced by previous correspondence). The applicant acted with fairness, seeking to expedite the process as long as it benefited the creditors and did not harm the debtors. The applicant always expressed agreement and was unwilling to argue over jurisdiction. However, the accountants regarded the applicant as someone easy to deal with. When they first published the advertisement for the auction of Huang's movable and immovable property, they did not inform the applicant and published the advertisement solely in the name of the liquidators of Gongfa Company. The applicant specifically questioned them in a letter due to their responsibility. Only then did they jointly publish the announcement (as evidenced by various newspapers). After the bidding opened on July 8th, the parties reviewed the bids together and agreed that all the bids were valid except for the West Warehouse Road property, which was valued too low (as evidenced by the joint signed review form). They should have separately notified the bidders to expedite the transaction. The applicant was proceeding in accordance with the law and there was nothing improper. The accountants initially urged the applicant to issue letters of notification but did not notify the bidders themselves. Now, they are blaming the applicant as one of the obstacles, which is incomprehensible. Also, July 16th was the first day of bidding. The day before, someone came to the applicant's office and informed the applicant's staff that the accounting firm was not issuing bid forms or accepting security deposits. Although the person's address was unknown and it was difficult to investigate, on the morning of the bidding, the applicant received a phone call from a bidder who said that the accounting firm's staff claimed that the accountant would not arrive until 12:00 noon and refused to issue bid forms or accept security deposits, leading to a dispute. The applicant, for the sake of the overall situation, telegraphed the accounting firm's staff to accompany the bidders to the applicant's office to handle the matter. The accounting firm's staff member Zhang Xing accompanied bidders Ding Qihong, Ge Jisheng, and Miao Hongchang. They stated that the accountant had indeed not arrived. The applicant issued bid forms and collected security deposits on behalf of the accountant, and Zhang Xing signed the temporary receipt to acknowledge the seriousness of the matter. The facts are clear and cannot be denied. The applicant sent a letter to the accountant on the same day proposing four measures, which was a necessary step at the time. The report stated, "If someone came to pay a security deposit, how could no one have heard in a small room?" This statement is somewhat embellished. As for whether the accountants worked more than ten hours a day, it is not something the applicant should inquire about. However, the accountants did not arrive before 11:00 AM that morning, as admitted by the firm's staff member Zhang Xing. The applicant, for the sake of the overall situation and friendship, offered sincere advice with the four measures and did not have ulterior motives. However, the accountants also cited this as an obstacle, which is a misunderstanding. The accountants had long harbored the intention to dispose of Huang's estate alone and did not hesitate to violate the court order, submitting a unilateral presentation to overturn the public auction and monopolize power. This resulted in Your Court's order to rescind the auction and seek a private sale. Public auctions are a transparent method, while private sales inevitably involve secrecy. Take the private sale of the Great World as an example. The Great World was the only valuable asset in Gongfa Company's assets. The lawyers representing the various creditors and the accountants had previously discussed a minimum auction price of 1.25 million, which was published in the newspapers. However, the result was that it was not publicly bid on, nor was it advertised for competitive sale. Instead, through a mysterious private sale method, a buyer was obtained who would pay 700,000 in installments, which was more than 550,000 less than the original minimum price, which is shocking. Regarding this point, the Huang family, as shareholders of Gongfa Company, should reserve the right to assert their legal rights in the future. However, the applicant, lacking the direct authority to interfere with Gongfa Company's liquidation affairs, has no power to make the claim and can only watch helplessly. It is strange that the lawyers representing the creditors, who are supposed to protect the creditors' interests, are actively interfering with the sale of Huang's estate but are indifferent to the sale of Gongfa Company's assets. The reason for this is worth pondering deeply. This private sale method is sufficient to cause external criticism and disputes between creditors and debtors, which is obvious. Although the applicant is foolish, he is unwilling to sell Huang's assets in his own area of responsibility and have the same phenomenon as the Great World occur. He will say everything he knows and say it to the fullest extent. Therefore, for the two auctions, he believes that the assets that have been reviewed and confirmed and for which the successful bidders have been notified should still be accepted by those bidders who pay the price and accept the assets to preserve credibility. For the assets that have not been reviewed and confirmed or have not been bid on, he believes that the methods of advertising for competitive sale or public auction should be used (the methods are detailed in the attached opinion letter). This would be sufficient to demonstrate impartiality, avoid private corruption, and ensure speed and avoid losses. Furthermore, this property is Huang Chu Jiu's personal property, which was approved for the liquidation of personal debts from the estate, not Gongfa Company's assets. According to the court order of March 30th, the responsibility for disposal and debt repayment naturally falls on the agent of the Huang family. This court order still has the liquidator seek to sell the assets, as if referring to Huang's family's liquidator. The applicant should be responsible for it. As if referring to the liquidator of Gongfa Company, it seems difficult for the liquidator of Gongfa Company to be responsible for the property that Gongfa Company does not own. Based on the interpretation of the word "still", it still agrees with the court's intent on March 30th, which is clear. In short, since the court order of March 30th has not expired, the accountant acted against the court order of March 30th with an independent behavior. If it is not an intentional encroachment on the duties of others, but a mistaken idea that the liquidator of Gongfa Company and the liquidator of Huang's family are the same (the rights and duties are detailed in the attached opinion), this is particularly confusing to the applicant. (2) Objection to the statement of lawyer Jiang Yiping representing the creditors of Gongfa Company: The liquidation in this case is of Huang Chu Jiu's estate and debts, as clearly indicated in Your Court's order of March 30th. Gongfa Company's position in this case is merely as one of the ordinary creditors. As for Gongfa Company's creditors, they have no direct creditor-debtor relationship with Huang (detailed reasons are in the attached opinion). According to the law, there is absolutely no room for interference. However, the lawyers dared to violate the law and infringe upon rights. Unless there is a different intention, why would they do this? Based on the above, and with the attached legal opinion, it is requested that Your Court approve the approval of the successful bidders who have been audited and confirmed and conduct public competitive bidding or public auction, to demonstrate fairness and prevent private corruption. This is for the public benefit. Respectfully submitted."

Contributed to the Hometown

▲ Intolerable to the Bandit Party

▲ Zhang Jinmao Died Tragically

A few days ago, multiple households were robbed by bandits in Wan Dou area, Gaoqiao Town, Pudong. In order to ensure the safety of the community, the 4th Section of the 5th District, due to the generous reward for capturing the bandit party, employed the local bailiff Shen Guanlin and the civilian Zhang Jinmao to assist in the investigation. They discovered that Ni Erlang, Zhu Jinhua, and Jin Fa, from Chongming, were indeed part of the bandit gang. They reported this to the police, who arrested and handed them over to the authorities. Although this contributed to the safety of the community, the bandit party held a grudge. A few days ago, Zhang Jinmao suddenly disappeared. Two days later, a foot was seen sticking out of the water near the Xiaoshi Bridge. The local bailiff Shen Guanlin went to investigate and saw that the trousers were made of Yunsha material. He pulled the body out of the water and found three large stones pressing on it. After removing the stones, he pulled the body out and recognized it as Zhang Jinmao's body. He notified Zhang Jinmao's father, Zhang Shaoyun, who mourned greatly at the scene. Yesterday, he filed a complaint with the local court, stating that he had been killed by the bandit party out of revenge and requesting justice. The local court dispatched Prosecutor Wu and the coroner to the scene. The coroner found that the corpse's eyes had been blinded with lime, there were knife wounds on the waist, and blood was coming out of the mouth. It was confirmed that the death was due to injuries. Photos were taken and the body was ordered to be collected for burial pending further investigation.

龔咸囡黨徒宋阿百陳木泉迎提歸案

Nanhui's notorious bandit Gong Xiannü and his gang members Song Abai, Zhu Danggen (Zhu Mengnan), Chen Muquan (Gong Jingen), etc., were captured by the French Concession police last month. They confessed to robbing Jin's family, a wealthy household in Shanghai, and were detained. The Nanhui authorities learned of this and ordered the Zhuqiao Security Corps to cooperate with the Fifth Public Security Bureau to retrieve the prisoners from the French Concession jail. After several negotiations, on July 19th, they extradited Song Abai, Chen Muquan, and Song Quanfu (six others had already been sent to Nanhui by the police for interrogation). Wang, a patrol officer from the Fifth Public Security Bureau, took them back. During interrogation, they confessed to the robberies. The following is a record of their confessions:

Song Abai confessed: I am twenty-eight years old and from the second Jia of the fifth Tuan. The Xue Haichun family robbery was orchestrated by Gong Xiannü. On the 27th day of the twelfth lunar month, Gong Xiannü initiated the plan and discussed the robbery with Chen Ada and me at Zhuqiao. On the evening of the Lantern Festival, Gong Xiannü led more than a dozen bandits, including Chen Ada, to carry out the robbery. Because I was a neighbor of the Xues, I feared being recognized, so I stayed in Zhuqiao. The next morning, Chen Ada gave me fourteen yuan (eight yuan in banknotes and six yuan in silver). I asked him why I only received fourteen yuan when the Xues were robbed of tens of thousands of gold. He said, "Gong Xiannü distributed it; it's none of my business." The robbery of the Pan Jiahong family in Henan was done by five people. In the robbery of the Heng family and the Mian family, each person received two quilts and three cloth shirts. The robbery of the Qiu Defu family was carried out by six of us, led by Gong Xiannü. We stole thirty-five yuan in banknotes, twenty-seven thousand copper coins, and a pair of gold rings. Each person received eight yuan. The Xu Shuying family robbery was last April. I did it with Chen Ada and six others. I received a fur coat and six yuan in silver. The box cannon and pistol found by the Zhuqiao Security Corps in the Ni Rongsheng, Wu Dian, and Jiang Zhiren kidnapping cases were issued by Gong Xiannü. The two pistols seized from Gui Xiaoqi and Zhu Yennü were also Gong Xiannü's. This is the truth.

Chen Muquan confessed: I am twenty-eight years old. My original name was Wang Yejin, but I took the surname Gong and was also known as Gong Jingen. I used the alias Chen Muquan at the police station. In the Yu Genlin and Zhang San kidnapping cases, Gong Xiannü instructed my cousin Wang Junsheng (who had already been executed with Yang A'gen) to tell me to borrow Gong Axiao's house to hide the hostage, which I did. I was responsible for providing food for the hostage. The robberies of the Jin family in the fifth Tuan, Xingqianqiao, Hedong, the Zhang Nanbing family in the fourth Jia of the fifth Tuan, and the Cai family in Waishatou were done with Chen Ada, Song Abai, Zhu Yennü, Gui Xiaoqi, Zhu Yemeimei, Zhu Mengnan, Zhou Zhitiao, etc. It is true that we repeatedly robbed and spent the stolen goods.

Song Quanfu confessed: I am thirty-two years old and from the second Jia of the fifth Tuan. I used to be in the Sichuan shipping business. Now I run an opium den at No. 87, Baxianfang, Baxianqiao, in the French Concession. Song Abai and others sometimes came to hang out and smoke opium. I really didn't know they were bandits; please have mercy.

The Zhuqiao Security Corps and the Fifth Public Security Bureau have jointly prepared a document to present to the Nanhui County Government for investigation and handling. The people of Zhuqiao are all delighted. It is also reported that various circles are preparing a joint petition to the Security Corps, requesting a thorough investigation.

市中心區領地餘波

Aftermath of Land Acquisition in the City Center Area

▲第一號抽籤人之聲明

▲Statement from the First Lottery Winner

The situation regarding land acquisition in the city center area has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. However, there are still issues with Zhang Zisong, the representative of Datongyuan Paper Company, who was the first lottery winner. This newspaper has received a letter from the company as follows: "To whom it may concern, our company bid for land in the city center area. Due to Director Zhu's discriminatory methods against our company and other lottery winners, our company's right to select land was unreasonably deprived. After the dispute arose, our company immediately sent a letter to the bureau questioning this, but has not received a reply to this day. We have read in various newspapers that the first lottery winner did not bring enough funds and only acquired one plot, which is not in line with the facts at the time. Therefore, we are providing a brief account of what happened. My colleagues and I, feeling the difficulty of living in Shanghai, gathered a group of friends and organized a group to bid for land in the city center area of Shanghai. In accordance with the Land Bureau's land acquisition notice, at 7:00 AM on July 21st, we sent designated representative Zhang Zisong, accompanied by manager Zhu Xiaoqin, to the Land Bureau to bid. We waited until about 10:00 AM (originally scheduled for 8:00 AM) when the lottery began. There were a total of 500 lottery numbers. At around 11:00 AM, Zhang Zisong drew the first number. He then signed his name under the number one on the signature book, and indicated that he intended to acquire four plots. At this time, the lottery was not yet complete, but five or six staff members of the Land Bureau suddenly rushed Zhang Zisong inside. Zhang was surrounded and could not go outside the lottery room to report to the manager and arrange for her to come inside. Later, the staff members of the bureau instructed him to choose which plots and urged him to quickly pay the land fees, pointing to the 5,000 yuan in silver he had brought and declaring that he was only allowed to acquire a little over ten mu of land. Zhang Zisong immediately stated that the funds he had brought were sufficient to cover the cost of four plots, but because of the crowd, he was concerned about potential dangers. He said that he had separately carried the funds at the manager Zhu Xiaoqin's place, and she was also in the bureau and could be easily retrieved. He wanted to go outside the bureau to get the funds from Zhu, but the staff members of the bureau sternly stopped him. Zhang Zisong was young and timid (18 years old) and did not dare to speak up further. At that time, other land acquirers, such as Yu Xiangxian and Zhan Peilin, saw this situation and testified on his behalf, confirming that Zhang Zisong had enough funds stored with Zhu Xiaoqin, and petitioned on his behalf to allow him to acquire the land in accordance with the law. Thereupon, the staff members of the bureau agreed to fill out the application form for four plots. Zhang Zisong then selected plots 23, 24, 42, and 43. Just as he was about to finish filling out the form, the Shanghai Bank drew the second number. But Director Zhu suddenly arrived and said that he had telegraphed the municipal government for instructions, saying that the lottery winner had only brought 5,000 yuan when drawing the lottery and was not allowed to acquire four plots. Zhang Zisong reiterated the previous situation, but Director Zhu did not wait for him to finish and announced that the first lottery winner did not have enough funds and was disqualified. At this time, Zhu Xiaoqin had entered the bureau after hearing the news and immediately argued that Zhang Zisong, the representative of our company, did not bring insufficient funds, but that he was afraid of accidents and had stored the funds on her person. She said that she could pay the full amount immediately when the land was acquired and that according to the land acquisition method, there would be no problems with the time and procedures. She then presented the funds to the director (the bureau originally stipulated that the payment deadline was 4:00 PM on the same day). Director Zhu refused to accept and said that only the funds personally brought by Zhang Zisong when drawing the lottery could be used. Zhu Xiaoqin repeatedly argued, but Director Zhu only allowed her to acquire one plot and instructed her that otherwise, the right to acquire the land would be completely cancelled. At this time, the land acquirers in the bureau witnessed the situation and felt injustice on behalf of our company. They questioned the bureau, but Section Chief Hu of the bureau declared that he would send 100 to 200 police officers to the bureau to suppress them. Zhu Xiaoqin and Zhang Zisong, seeing the firm attitude of the bureau and the urgency of the situation, reluctantly complied with filling out the application form and acquired one plot. They still clearly stated to Director Zhu that they would reserve the remaining three plots pending a legal solution. Zhang Zisong then took the application form back to the cashier's office and paid 12,000 yuan in bank drafts and 375 yuan in silver. Because the Jiang drafts were not due until the 23rd, they were not accepted. Zhu Xiaoqin then issued a blank check from Datongyuan Paper Company to Yongfeng Bank for 12,000 yuan and presented it, obtaining a receipt for the payment, and was then able to acquire plot 24 and leave. This was what happened on that day. Our company's land acquisition procedures were handled in accordance with the land acquisition method promulgated by the municipal government and the land acquisition notice of the Land Bureau, without any violations. However, Director Zhu repeatedly changed the method, making it difficult for land acquirers to comply, and the various situations he confronted our company with were particularly appalling. Our company was forced to submit to the strict authority of the administrative officials at the time. In addition to sending a letter to the director of the bureau questioning him the next day, we are providing details to clarify the truth."

The postal authorities stated that for all parcels destined for south of Yanmenguan in Shanxi or to various locations within the Inner Great Wall, an additional fee is required. These parcels are now being transferred via Datong.

美豐銀行營業情形

The Business Situation of the American Oriental Banking Corporation

The American Oriental Banking Corporation, in the first half of 1930, showed a satisfactory progress in the business accounts of all the head and branch offices in Shanghai and Tianjin. During this half-year, its net profit reached Shanghai silver dollars 414,770.04. This number is distributed as follows, including: payment of income tax in 1930, silver dollars 42,282.62, depreciation of property and equipment, 5,172.41, preferred stock dividend, 40,000.00, time stock dividend, interest on ordinary shares at 10%, 127,795.03, transferred to the next period account, 198,926.98, 414,177.04. Because the results of all business operations during this half-year are very satisfactory, and each department is developing, the board of directors decided to increase the issuance of ordinary shares, calculated in Shanghai local silver dollars. If the issuance of increased ordinary shares is issued, the capital surplus and undistributed profits in the bank will exceed 6 million silver dollars. The new shares must be purchased by the old shareholders, and if there is a surplus, it can be sold. This matter will be completed on July 31, 1931. Because the business is developing, all office space is insufficient for use and needs to be expanded. All plans have been prepared and a contract has been signed with the construction factory to immediately expand the bank building by 1,500 square feet. This expansion plan can be completed within a few months.

華昌油漆並無毒質

Huachang Paint is Non-Toxic

▲浙民廳誤會查抄

▲Zhejiang Provincial Government Misunderstands and Confiscates

▲國貨會電請發還

▲National Products Association Telegraphs for Return

The China National Products Maintenance Association believes that the sanitary paint produced by its member Huachang Manufacturing Factory has been falsely accused and mistakenly reported to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, resulting in the confiscation of products. It previously sent a letter to inquire about the matter. It has now received a reply from the factory reporting the details. The 19th meeting of the 20th Executive Supervisory Committee resolved to telegraph to the Zhejiang Provincial Government and the Department of Civil Affairs to uphold justice and conduct a thorough investigation to clear the name of the national product and facilitate its sales. The original telegram stated: (omitted above) According to the factory's reply, the sanitary paint produced by our company is made by chemically combining useless scraps of leather and water, and does not contain any opium. It has been approved by the Central Health Testing Institute, registered by the Customs and Industry Department's National Trademark Registration Bureau, and approved by the Flying Orangutan trademark, and protected by official orders from various provincial, municipal, and county governments. The Zhejiang Department of Civil Affairs also sent personnel to the factory along with Chinese and Western staff from the Yangshupu Patrol Room of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau to investigate and found no prohibited items. Western staff from the patrol room also certified that the factory has been operating for many years, manufacturing oils and does not contain opium. The concession authorities allow it to operate, and the products are inspected by the customs before export, otherwise how can they be sold at home and abroad? The Zhejiang authorities were misled by false reports, resulting in a misunderstanding, which will undoubtedly be cleared up. However, those who falsely accuse national products should be investigated. Please telegraph to prove it, request to uphold justice and conduct a thorough investigation, and so on. When the factory joined our association, it was required to send personnel to investigate and confirm that it was manufacturing paint and did not mix any toxic substances. This is evidenced by the inspection certificate of the Central Health Testing Institute, customs registration, and the testimony of patrol room staff, which is a legitimate business and there is no doubt about it. Therefore, we are specifically telegraphing to Your Excellency to conduct a thorough investigation,

return the confiscated products, and restore business operations (omitted below).

一産三孩

One Birth, Three Children

Luo Adi, a Jiangbei native residing in Dongshi, Zhoujiaqiao, West Shanghai, is 30 years old and works at Rongmao Sawmill. His wife, Wang, is 23 years old and also works at Toyota Yarn Factory. They have been married for five years and have not had any children. In March of last year, Luo was eagerly hoping for a child, and Wang suddenly became pregnant. Later, she gradually felt bloated. Unexpectedly, after ten months, there was no sign of childbirth. Her husband feared she was ill and consulted a doctor, who confirmed she was pregnant and had no illness. By this year, her abdomen felt even more enlarged, like a gourd weighing five piculs. Luo was even more anxious. However, Wang continued to work and live as usual. At 1:00 AM the day before yesterday, Wang suddenly felt abdominal pain. Her husband knew that she was about to give birth and prepared. When the clock struck seven, she indeed gave birth to a baby boy. In an instant, two more children were born. The sound of their cries shook the house. Luo was shocked and surprised. All three children were male, lively as usual, and had no strange features. Later, Luo heard superstitious words from neighbors, fearing they were monsters, and abandoned the three children outside the door, letting people watch. This caused a sensation and attracted onlookers from far and wide, who all said that the three children had no strange features and urged Luo to take them back and care for them. However, a birth of three children is indeed a rare event.

菜販跌入小河溺斃

Vegetable Vendor Falls into River and Drowns

▲亦受大雨之害

▲Also a Victim of Heavy Rain

Wang Quanfu, a local villager, 24 years old, lived in the Jijiaku near Zhongshan Road, Caojiadu, West Shanghai. He was a farmer. Due to the continuous heavy rain in recent days, he was unable to work. Every morning, he dug up the vegetables he grew and carried them to the market to sell. Yesterday at around 3:40 AM, Wang still carried vegetables from his home, planning to go to Caojiadu Town. At that time, the heavy rain had slightly subsided, and the dawn was breaking. He hadn't gone far when he reached the small wooden bridge on the small river near Zhongshan Road. The bridge was submerged by water. Wang still stepped on the bridge in the water. He was careless and slipped into the river. Because he couldn't swim, he sank and died instantly. Later, his body floated up and was spotted by villagers, who reported it to his family, who rushed to retrieve it and prepared a coffin for burial.

Zhao Guanqing previously hired a lawyer to sue Bei Runsheng, Zhao Pinhou, Zhao Zhulin, etc. in the civil court of the French Concession Court for failing to repay the principal and interest of the Yisheng firm's advances, totaling more than 1 million, and was sentenced. Zhao, dissatisfied with the judgment, filed reasons and requested a retrial, which was approved by the judge. The defendant failed to appear twice, and was ordered to summon again for verification. Yesterday, when the summons was due again, both the plaintiff and the defendant, accompanied by their respective lawyers, stated in court that the case had been settled and requested that the case be dismissed. Judge Zhu ruled that since both parties had reached an agreement, the case was approved for dismissal, and the court fees were to be borne equally by both parties.

謀生無着爲盜

Became a Thief Due to Lack of Livelihood

▲陳仰蘇判押五年

▲Chen Yangsu Sentenced to Five Years in Prison

The bandit Chen Yangsu, on the night of the 22nd of last month, and Zhou Er, who is at large, tried to rob people on Xujiahui Road in the French Concession. Just as Xu Qintang, a French Concession detective, came to inspect and ordered them to stop, he was about to search them when Zhou shot Xu in the left arm, injuring him and causing him to fall to the ground. At that time, the detectives only arrested Chen Yangsu, and Zhou escaped. Yesterday, the police sent Chen, the thief, to the criminal court of the French Concession Court for trial. The police chief first reported the previous situation. When questioned, Chen Yangsu confessed that he was from Funing and had not been in Shanghai for long. He had no way to make a living. Last month, he met Zhou Er, a fellow villager, on the road. He explained to him the plight of his livelihood. Zhou said that he would help him rob people on the road, that is, rob and live like a pig. The people had no choice but to agree. The first time, Zhou and his wife, a woman named Xiao Laohan, invited Chen and two others to go to Jin Shenfu Road, where they met a certain Jia. Zhou threatened him with a pistol, and his wife Xiao Laohan took the initiative to strip off his clothes and rob him. Chen kept watch nearby. The next day, Chen was given three yuan. The second time, the three went to Xujiahui to rob a certain person's clothes and other items. And until the third time, Chen and Zhou

were walking along Xujiahui Road and were searched by detectives. Zhou opened fire to resist arrest, and the people were arrested. That's the truth. The Chinese and Western officials sentenced Chen to five years in the Western prison, and he will be deported from the concession forever after his term expires.

雉妓跳出火坑

Prostitute Escapes from Hell

▲五年來備受苦楚

▲Suffered for Five Years

Zhang Xiaomei, a 19-year-old woman from Liuhe, is quite beautiful. When she was young, due to the poverty of her family, her parents arranged for her to be a child bride to the son of Wang Arong. She passed the door immediately. Later, when she was 14 years old, Wang Arong brought her to Shanghai and rented a house at No. 8 and a half, Rongqing Lane, Sixth Avenue, in the Public Concession, and opened a brothel. In that year, she was forced to do business. If she was slightly dissatisfied, she would be beaten. She could not agree. She has been doing it for five years. However, because she was weak and often sick, the old madam did not show any sympathy and still asked her to receive guests. If she did not obey, she would be beaten severely. The suffering was extreme. It was a living hell. In recent days, she has been suffering from illness and fever, and the rain has been falling for almost ten days, and there is nowhere to find customers. She asked the madam to let her rest for a few days, but Arong refused and beat her severely, causing her body to be covered with bruises, and still drove her out to find customers. At more than 11:00 the night before last, Xiaomei was complaining on the road. Taking advantage of the old madam's unpreparedness, she fled to Liu Fen Lane in the city and asked where the police station was, intending to seek help from the station. Patrolman Jiang Zhenshan inquired about the situation and immediately took her to the First Branch of the Second District. After Director Xu inquired whether she had any relatives, Xiaomei said that she had been sold to Wang Arong's son as a child bride by her parents since she was a child, so she had no relatives and did not want to engage in this flesh business anymore. She cried as she spoke, begging for relief. Director Xu, knowing the situation, decided to send her to the Public Security Bureau and then to the Women and Children Relief Association.

Letter Received

To the Esteemed Editor,

I recently read in various newspapers, in the local news section, about the case of Zhao Guanqing suing Bei Runsheng, regarding the resolution reached today. The facts reported do not quite align with what actually occurred. Upon investigation, my clients, Bei Runsheng and his brothers Zhao Zhulin, are close relatives of the plaintiff Zhao Guanqing. Although they were involved in a lawsuit due to a momentary disagreement, Zhao Guanqing has now asked relatives and friends to mediate and voluntarily signed an agreement to settle the dispute, relinquishing all claims. On the side of my clients, they also accepted the advice of relatives and friends and provided financial assistance, paying 50,000 silver dollars. Today, their original lawyer requested the withdrawal of the review in court at the Public Concession Court. Furthermore, according to the evidence from both parties, the lawyer is Jin Yu, whose signature is well-known among our lawyers, and not lawyer Huang Huansheng. We have always admired your newspaper's commitment to recording everything it hears. I am sending this letter requesting a correction. With best wishes for your well-being.

Respectfully,

Lawyer Zou Shengzu, July 27th

To the Esteemed Editor,

On July 26th, your newspaper's local news section published a news item titled "Shanghai-Xiamen Wireless Communication Disconnected." I was extremely surprised upon reading it. After the recovery of domestic transmission rights from companies such as Da Dongbei, our station anticipated a surge in telegram traffic to Xiamen, Fuzhou, and other locations. We had previously submitted a request to install additional equipment on both sides, which was approved to facilitate the clearance of various cases. Although there has been persistent rainfall recently, all telegrams to Xiamen have been relayed by our station and delivered promptly as usual. There have been no instances of damage or disconnection, nor is there any reason to return received commercial telegrams. The facts are as they are and do not need to be concealed. We are concerned that inaccurate rumors may lead to misunderstandings, so we are sending this special letter to inform you. We hope you will investigate and make corrections to maintain our public relations. Addressed to the Shen Bao Newspaper Office, from the Shanghai Wireless Telegraph General Station of the Ministry of Communications, July 27th.

Book and Newspaper Reviews

A Brief History of the Shanghai Concessions

— Tiehua

Compiled and translated by Cen Dezhang, sold by World Da Dong

At a time when the entire nation is united in its efforts to recover the concessions, I believe that this compilation and translation of "A Brief History of the Shanghai Concessions" is a very good contribution. Therefore, I am introducing it here to the people of the country as reference material and historical discussion.

Regarding the history of the Shanghai concessions, I am afraid there are many people who do not understand it clearly. We only know that the origin of the concessions was due to the failure of the Opium War and the opening of treaty ports. But the details of how it happened and the gradual expansion, I think all Chinese people should pay attention to. This book tells us all the things we urgently need to know.

This book was compiled and translated by Mr. Cen Dezhang based on A Short History of Shanghai by Morse, supplemented by various books and interviews with elders. The entire book has more than 360 pages and is supplemented by a chronology of major events in the Shanghai concessions, starting from the signing of the Treaty of Nanjing between China and Britain on August 29th of the 22nd year of Daoguang in the Qing Dynasty until the 19th year of the Republic of China. The major events of the concessions are listed in a chronological table. The entire book is divided into 28 chapters, including the signing of treaties and trade, the establishment of concessions, red-headed city occupation, the revision of regulations, the Taiping Rebellion, the scale of municipal administration, construction overview, the Siming Public Institute incident, the development of transportation, the revision of regulations, the foundation of education, the fiftieth anniversary celebration, the industrial revolution, the expansion of concessions, the Boxer Rebellion in the Gengzi year, the Boxer Protocol in the Xin Chou year, the big commotion at the public hall, building roads beyond the boundaries, the Wuchang Uprising, raising troops to fight against Yuan Shikai, the European war, resisting the attached laws, the Lincheng train robbery, the Qi-Lu war, the May Thirtieth Movement, etc. Each chapter is further divided into dozens of subsections. The historical events of the concessions are exhaustively covered. This kind of collection is really not easy.

The whole book is very long, and it is difficult to list everything in detail. Here is a brief introduction to one or two points regarding the origin of the concessions:

"Shanghai was declared a treaty port on November 14th of the 22nd year of Daoguang in the Qing Dynasty (1843). Pottinger did not mention concessions in the treaty, and the matter was left to Balfour and the Shanghai Daotai to resolve through mutual consultation. At that time, the Chinese officials opposed the establishment of concessions, thinking that selling land would violate national laws. Later, the sale was changed to perpetual lease, and the tenants paid an annual rent. At that time, the price of land was about 15 to 35 strings of cash per mu, while the price charged to foreigners was 50 to 60 strings (about 50 to 60 silver dollars). The annual rent was about 1 string and 500 cash."

Regarding the boundaries of the concessions:

"The four boundaries of the concessions were not initially defined. Roughly, the east was bounded by the Huangpu River, the south by the Yangjingbang, and the north by what is now Beijing Road, while the west had no clear boundaries. Later, boundary roads were designated as the boundaries, namely the current Henan Road. The land initially included in the concessions was 150 acres (English acres)..."

During the Xianfeng and Tongzhi periods, the book contains a vivid description of the life of foreigners in Shanghai: "Every day, they would go to the racecourse to test their horses, with a leisurely attitude. Those who liked to engage in Qingtan (pure conversation) would gather at the Huangpu Bund. At that time, the Bund Road was very wide and equal to the concessions. In the morning, porters gathered, and as the sun set, foreign merchants and local women strolled leisurely, creating a harmonious scene. All those who came east with the envoys recognized Shanghai as a paradise in China."

Since the Taiping Army rose and approached Shanghai, the Qing court did not hesitate to ask foreigners for help and joined the battle. The Changsheng Army (Ever Victorious Army) monument in the Bund Park is a tribute established by Li Hongzhang. The rogue foreigner Ward was the first to lead foreign troops to help the Qing court, so after his death in battle, his name was listed at the top of the monument.

Later, the scale of municipal administration gradually developed. The establishment of the Public Concession, and the merger of the British and American Concessions, implied the idea of changing the concessions into a free city. In other words, the Shanghai Concessions would be an independent republic. At that time, the British Consul Medhurst was still able to uphold justice, saying, "This piece of land originally belonged to China, but only allowed the contracting countries to exercise their consular jurisdiction here. It was never intended to abandon its sovereignty over the land and people of China." British envoy Bruce also objected, saying, "The nature of the Shanghai Concessions is neither cession nor lease. All the land we own still belongs to the territory of China." However, after more than 80 years of delay, what kind of phenomenon has it become now?

The collection in the book is very rich. To list them all individually is really not as good as reading through the entire book. So I don't want to spend any more time writing. However, the story of the origin of Jishi Fei Er Road is very interesting: "The name Jishi Fei Er Road has an anecdotal story. It is said that a Portuguese gentleman, while passing by the Hongkou Circus, heard a woman crying sadly in a tent. So he redeemed her and sent her to a American missionary for upbringing. The woman later learned to talk to a gentleman and went to the United States to study. After returning to China, she married the gentleman. The woman's name was Jishi, so the area was jokingly called Jishi Fei Er." There are many such records in the book, and there is no need to list them all to take up space.

In short, this book, although called A Brief History of the Shanghai Concessions, its content is already specific and is indeed a history book that our people must read. When the reporter carried it on the tram to read, many people eagerly asked about the place of publication, which shows that many people pay attention to and are more eager for the history of the concessions. Then, the value of this book and the meaning of its publication do not need me to talk anymore.

The price of this book is two yuan, or maybe it can be discounted to 1.9 yuan. I think that when it is reprinted, the font can be reduced, the paper can be reduced, and the price can be reduced in order to popularize it. I dare to say this to the compiler Mr. Cen.

The Three Principles of the People and Population Policy

— Shih Huai

By Chen Changheng

I have read many books about population issues and population policies written in Chinese. Some are too simple, and some are not simple, but they are too old. Several seem better, but unfortunately, they are translated from foreign countries. Their background and position are not China, and it seems that there is a layer of separation for me personally. It can be regarded as a good book in the current publications on population issues and population policies by our own people.

Page 20

I think that apart from this book "The Three Principles of the People and Population Policy" that I am going to introduce now, I cannot find another one to compare.

The author of this book, Mr. Chen Changheng, is currently a member of the Legislative Yuan of the National Government. He has been engaged in the study of population issues for at least ten years. His most important work is "On Chinese Population," a book introducing the Malthusian theory and opposing neo-Malthusianism. Later, in the "Eastern Miscellany," "Modern Review," and "China Review Weekly," there were papers on population issues. This book is a collection of his research over the past ten years on the quantity of China's population and the theories of natural environment, social environment, and heredity on racial evolution in the West, as well as the universal fertility revolution created by his research.

The book is divided into twelve chapters, totaling 342 pages, which can be said to be a masterpiece. The titles of each chapter are as follows: Chapter 1, the overall classification of Mr. Sun Yat-sen's population theory; Chapter 2, the population issue as a prerequisite for the thorough realization of the Three Principles of the People; Chapter 3, a new estimate of the total population of China; Chapter 4, how to maintain the population density that "exceeds the species principle"; Chapter 5, population density and life standards; Chapter 6, population policies regarding quality; Chapter 7, the relationship between the natural environment and racial evolution; Chapter 8, the relationship between genetic advantages and disadvantages and racial evolution; Chapter 9, the relationship between good and bad habits, superior and inferior culture, and racial evolution; Chapter 10, the positive significance, philanthropy, and scientific basis of the fertility revolution; Chapter 11, the specific plan of the fertility revolution and the guiding facilities that the government should have; Chapter 12, conclusion.

The book strongly criticizes foreign scholars such as Willcox, who believe that the household survey of the Ministry of Civil Affairs in the second year of Xuantong, "the national population is 320 million," is accurate. He cited many counties that underreported households and the inaccuracy of the number of people per household being 43. As a result, he revised the population in the second year of Xuantong to be 385 million. He also calculated that the average population growth rate in China in the past 18 years is 11 per thousand, which is slightly higher than the world's average population growth rate of 8 per thousand. From this, he further calculated that the total population of our country now should be 470 million. Aren't we often saying 400 million? He is now overturning this old saying. He tells us that the current population of China is too large. The population suitable for our current situation is 250 million, and our population doubles every 60 years.

Mr. Chen Changheng strongly argues for the relationship between population quantity and population quality. A saturated population density mostly has a counter-selection effect in its natural selection process. Therefore, he believes that a government should formulate a timely population density. In this timely population density, the highest life standard can be maintained.

The universal fertility revolution is the population policy created by Mr. Chen to formulate a timely population density. The universal fertility revolution has three meanings: (1) It can avoid the focus of international competition, equalize the differences in international culture, and promote the world's great unity; (2) It can reduce the time difference between joy and sorrow, the geographical difference, and the human difference to increase the value of life and human happiness; (3) It can reduce the difference in gender and the number of men and women to maintain the quantitative balance of the sexes and promote the common happiness of the sexes.

His specific plan is: (1) Abolish the patriarchal early marriage and concubinage; (2) Implement one-flower and two-flower policies (i.e., one boy and one girl, and two boys and two girls); (3) The fertility revolution should be mainly guided and nurtured by the government.

Finally, I quote the conclusion of this book as the end of this article: "...We must be under the guidance of such an approachable, lovely, admirable, and respectable leader. Only then can the Chinese nation be truly saved. Our blue sky, white sun, flawless jade, supreme and divine, and forever the new utopia of East Asia can be safely and soundly produced. Only then can our people forever enjoy a more noble civilization, more abundant and healthier, more just and pure, more loving and free, more complete and beautiful, and more glorious and sacred common life and personal life. Our future, as beautiful as a tapestry, is a new utopia that is the new kingdom of heaven shared by all our people, and it is the road that we must take from 'one person in China' to 'one family in the world'."

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Reviews

(1) The text is limited to the introduction of the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all books and newspapers on politics, economics, law, science, education, etc. are included in the introduction. However, books and newspapers without connection will not be introduced.

(2) Books are limited to the latest works of new writers at home and abroad and attached pictures related to the text.
